Salam in Measured-by-Dimension Items: Cloth Conditions and Proof
Specifies conditions for Salam in cloth and responds to a qiyas objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required specifications for Salam in cloth (length, width, thickness) and explain why dimensions suffice using the Hanafi qiyas argument.

Core Idea
Salam in cloth is valid by specifying length, width, and thickness; for silk, weight must also be specified.

Salam is a forward sale of non-existent goods, an exception to the normal prohibition of selling what you do not possess. This passage explains how the Hanafi school extends this exception to items measured by dimension (madhru‘), such as cloth, provided their key attributes are precisely stated. We will examine the required specifications, the special case of silk, and the logical proof (qiyas) that supports the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item and its required specifications
For cloth, the buyer must stipulate the length, width, and thickness (coarseness/smoothness). These define the item's value and prevent future disputes.
Thickness is expressed by the term 'ruq'ah' in the text.
2
Note the exception for silk
For silk cloth, the weight must also be specified because its value varies significantly with weight, unlike ordinary cloth.
This is a ruling from later Hanafi commentators like al-Shimni and al-Barjandi.
3
Locate the anticipated objection
The text raises an objection: Salam is an exception to qiyas (sale of non-existent) and the hadith only mentions measured (kayl) and weighed (wazn) items; so should it be restricted to those?
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith's mention is exemplary (tamthil), not exclusive (takhsis). The underlying reason (illah) is the ability to precisely specify the item, which applies equally to dimensioned goods.
This is a classic application of qiyas with the illah of 'imkan al-dabt' (possibility of precise definition).
5
Confirm the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon position is that Salam in cloth is valid with the stated specifications, and for silk, weight must be added. This is supported by zahir al-riwayah and later fatawa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والمذروع كالثوب مُبيَّناً طولُهُ وعرضُهُ ورقعته) : أي غلظته وسخافته. وقول ابن أبان أصح؛ لأنَّ المعقود عليه هو المسلم فيه، وإنما يصحح العقد في محلّ أوجب فيه، وصححه في «الهداية» (۱) و «كمال الدراية»، و«النهى» وغيرها، ورجح في «الفتح»(۳) قول أبي بكر الأعمش . وإن شئت التفصيل فارجع إليه وإلى «البحر » ) ، وهذا الخلافُ فيما إذا أسلم غير شيء من النقدين في أحدهما، وأمَّا إذا أسلم أحدهما في الآخر، فإنّه لا يجوز بالإجماع ؛ لأنَّ النقد بانفراده يحرِّمُ النَّسأ كذا في كمال الدراية (٥). وأما الفلوس فلم تخلق للثمنية، فلو أسلم في الفلوس عدداً جاز، وهو ظاهرُ الرواية عن الشيخين، وعن محمد الله : أنه لا يجوز ، كذا في «الفتاوى المنصورية». وفي «الذخيرة»: منهم من قال جوازُ السَّلم في الفلوس، ذكره البرجندي . ١ ] قوله : والمذروع كالثوب... الخ ؛ أي صح السَّلَمُ فيما يعلم قدره وصفتُهُ كالمذروع ، إذا بين طوله وعرضه وغلظته وسخافته كالثياب ؛ لأنَّ مقدار المالية في الثياب ونحوها معلوم بذكر هذه الأشياء، والتفاوت بغيرها يسير فلا يضر؛ لأنه لا يفضي إلى المنازعة المانعة من التسليم والتسلم، وهذا في غير الحرير. أما في الحرير فلا بد فيه من ذكر الوزن أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ قيمة الثوب منه تختلفُ باختلاف وزنه ؛ صرح به العلامة الشمني ) ، والبر جندي وغيرهمـا مـن أصحاب الشروح والفتاوى. فإن قيل : ينبغي أن لا يجوز السَّلَمُ في المذروعات ؛ لأنَّ السَّلَم ثبت بخلاف القياس؛ لأنه بيع المعدوم، والنص ورد في الكيلي والوزني. قلنا : النص ورد بذكر الكيل والوزن تمثيلاً لا تخصيصاً، والمعنى هو ما يمكن ضبطه وتمييزه عن غيره، ولا شك أن المذروع كذلك؛ لأنَّ الضابط يذكره. ثم هذا الخلاف إذا أسلم في أحد النقدين، أما إذا أسلم النقد في النقد الآخر فلا يجوز بالإجماع.
(And the measured by dimension like cloth, specifying its length, width, and thickness): i.e., its coarseness and smoothness. And the statement of Ibn Aban is more correct because the subject of the contract is the muslam fih, and he validates the contract in a place where it is required, and it was validated in al-Hidayah and Kamal al-Diraya and al-Nihaya and others, and in al-Fath the statement of Abu Bakr al-A'mash was preferred. And if you want the detail, refer to it and to al-Bahr. And this difference is when one makes Salam in something other than the two currencies in one of them. As for when one makes Salam of one of them in the other, then it is not permissible by consensus. As for fulus, they were not created for being a price, so if one makes Salam in fulus by number, it is permissible, and that is the apparent narration from the two shaykhs, and from Muhammad that it is not permissible, as in al-Fatawa al-Mansuriyya. And in al-Dhakhira: some of them said the permissibility of Salam in fulus, mentioned by al-Barjandi. 1] His saying: 'And the measured by dimension like cloth...'; i.e., Salam is valid in what is known in its quantity and quality like something measured by dimension, if its length, width, coarseness, and smoothness are specified, like clothes; because the value of clothes and the like is known by mentioning these things, and the difference in other aspects is insignificant, so it does not harm; because it does not lead to dispute preventing delivery and receipt. And this is in other than silk. As for silk, it is necessary to mention the weight as well because the value of a cloth from it differs with difference in its weight; stated by al-Shimni, al-Barjandi, and others among the authors of commentaries and fatawa. If it is said: it ought that Salam is not valid in things measured by dimension because Salam is established contrary to qiyas; for it is a sale of a non-existent thing, and the text came in measured and weighed items. We say: the text came mentioning measure and weight as examples, not as specification, and the meaning is what can be precisely defined and distinguished from others, and there is no doubt that the thing measured by dimension is like that; because the person defining it mentions it. Then this difference is when one makes Salam in one of the two currencies. As for when one makes Salam of one currency in the other, it is not permissible by consensus.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding Salam in items measured by dimension (madhru'), specifically cloth. The author states that Salam is valid in cloth if its length, width, and thickness (coarseness/smoothness) are specified. He then notes a difference of opinion (intra-Hanafi) regarding Salam in dirhams and dinars, but that is covered in the previous lesson. Here, the focus is on the conditions for cloth. The author explains that specifying dimensions is sufficient because the value is known from them; minor variations do not lead to disputes. However, for silk, weight must also be mentioned because its value varies significantly with weight. The author then addresses a potential objection: Salam is an exception to qiyas (since it is a sale of non-existent goods), and the hadith only mentions measured (kayl) and weighed (wazn) items. The response is that the mention is exemplary, not exclusive; the underlying reason is the ability to precisely specify the item, which applies to dimensioned items as well. The author also reiterates the consensus forbidding Salam of one currency for another.

Key Terms
المذروع (al-madhru'): Items measured by dimension (length, width, thickness), like cloth.
رقعته (ruq'atuhu): Thickness or coarseness of cloth; part of the necessary specifications.
الحرير (al-harir): Silk; special rules apply for Salam in silk – weight must be specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What additional specification is required for Salam in silk cloth compared to ordinary cloth?
A) The color.
B) The weight.
C) The origin.
D) The brand.

Key Takeaway
For Salam in cloth, specify length, width, and thickness; for silk, also weight; the Hanafi school extends Salam to dimensioned items based on the illa of precise specification.

Salam in Measured Items: Analogical Extension via Qiyas Khafi
Analogical proof for salam in measured items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits salam in measured items (madhru'at) by applying qiyas khafi based on the possibility of equivalence (taswiyah) and state the extra condition for silk.

Core Idea
Salam in measured items is valid because equivalence in delivery is achievable by measurement, just as by volume or weight.

Salam (advance sale) is a special contract where the price is paid immediately and the commodity is delivered later. The Quran explicitly permits it for known volume and weight (kayl and wazn). But what about items measured by length, like cloth? The Hanafi school extends this permission using a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi). This lesson unpacks that reasoning, including the key condition of specifying dimensions, the special rule for silk, and the intra-Hanafi disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Original Permission (Asl)
The Quran (2:282) allows salam in makil (volume) and mawzun (weight). This is the established case (asl) with a clear ruling: permissible.
Quran: '…fa-sallim fi kaylin ma'lum wa waznin ma'lum.'
2
Extract the Effective Cause (Illah)
The reason (illah) for this permission is the possibility of equivalence (taswiyah) in delivery. Because the commodity can be precisely described by volume or weight, the buyer receives exactly what was agreed upon, avoiding dispute.
The illah is extracted via tahqiq al-manat from the wisdom behind the ruling.
3
Apply the Illah to the New Case (Far’)
Measured items (madhru'at) like cloth can also be precisely described—by length, width, and thickness. Thus, equivalence in delivery is achievable just as with volume/weight. Therefore, salam in measured items is valid via textual indication (dalālah).
For silk, weight must also be specified because value varies with weight.
4
Address the Objection
Some argue that salam is an exception to the rule (sale of non-existent) and the text only mentions kayl/wazn. The Hanafi response: the text's reason (illah) is general and not restricted to kayl/wazn; measurement (dhirā‘) provides the same precision.
This is an example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the illah is not explicit but derived from the text's purpose.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Validity
There is a difference among Hanafi scholars on the general validity of salam in measured items. Ibn Aban considers it valid; Abu Bakr al-A'mash rejects it. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that of Ibn Aban as stated in al-Hidayah and other works.
This dispute does not affect the operative ruling for fatwa, which follows the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

في محلّ أوجب فيه، وصححه في «الهداية» (۱) و «كمال الدراية»، و«النهى» وغيرها، ورجح في «الفتح»(۳) قول أبي بكر الأعمش .

وإن شئت التفصيل فارجع إليه وإلى «البحر » ) ، وهذا الخلافُ فيما إذا أسلم غير شيء من النقدين في أحدهما، وأمَّا إذا أسلم أحدهما في الآخر، فإنّه لا يجوز بالإجماع ؛ لأنَّ النقد بانفراده يحرِّمُ النَّسأ كذا في كمال الدراية (٥).
وأما الفلوس فلم تخلق للثمنية، فلو أسلم في الفلوس عدداً جاز، وهو ظاهرُ الرواية عن الشيخين، وعن محمد الله : أنه لا يجوز ، كذا في «الفتاوى المنصورية». وفي «الذخيرة»: منهم من قال جوازُ السَّلم في الفلوس، ذكره البرجندي . ١ ] قوله : والمذروع كالثوب... الخ ؛ أي صح السَّلَمُ فيما يعلم قدره وصفتُهُ كالمذروع ، إذا بين طوله وعرضه وغلظته وسخافته كالثياب ؛ لأنَّ مقدار المالية في الثياب ونحوها معلوم بذكر هذه الأشياء، والتفاوت بغيرها يسير فلا يضر؛ لأنه لا يفضي إلى المنازعة المانعة من التسليم والتسلم، وهذا في غير الحرير. أما في الحرير فلا بد فيه من ذكر الوزن أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ قيمة الثوب منه تختلفُ باختلاف وزنه ؛ صرح به العلامة الشمني ) ، والبر جندي وغيرهمـا مـن أصحاب
(٦)
الشروح والفتاوى. فإن قيل : ينبغي أن لا يجوز السَّلَمُ في المذروعات ؛ لأنَّ السَّلَم ثبت بخلاف القياس؛ لأنه بيع المعدوم، والنص ورد في الكيلي والوزني.
قلنا : يلحق المذروعات بهما بدلالة النص لِمَا أنَّ قولَه : «فليسلم في كـيـل معلوم ووزن معلوم»، إنما اقتضى الجواز في المكيل والموزون باعتبار إمكان التسوية في التسليم على ما وصف في المسلم فيه والتسوية كما يتحقق بالكيل كذلك يتحقق بالذرع ، فيجوزُ السَّلَمَ في المذروعات بطريقِ الدلالة، كذا في «الكفاية»).
And measured items (al-madhru') like cloth, specifying its length and width and thickness. And measured items like cloth, specifying its length and width and thickness: that is, its thickness and coarseness. And the statement of Ibn Aban is more correct because the object of the contract is the salaf item, and the contract is only validated in a place that necessitates it, and it was validated in al-Hidayah and Kamal al-Dirayah and al-Nihayah and others, and in al-Fath he preferred the statement of Abu Bakr al-A'mash. And if you wish detail, refer to it and to al-Bahr. And this disagreement is regarding when one pays for something other than one of the two numismatics (gold/silver) in one of them; but if one pays one of them in the other, it is not permissible by consensus because the numismatic alone prohibits deferment, as in Kamal al-Dirayah. As for copper coins (fulus), they were not created for being currency, so if one gives salaf in copper coins by number, it is permissible, and that is the apparent transmission from the two shaykhs, and from Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) that it is not permissible, as in al-Fatawa al-Mansuriyyah. And in al-Dhakhirah: some said the permissibility of salam in copper coins, mentioned by al-Birjandi. His statement: 'and measured items like cloth' etc., i.e., salam is valid in what is known in quantity and description like measured items, when its length and width and thickness and coarseness like cloth are specified, because the amount of value in cloth and similar is known by mentioning these things, and variation in others is slight so it does not harm because it does not lead to dispute that prevents delivery and receipt. This is for non-silk. As for silk, it is necessary to also mention weight because the value of a garment of it differs with its weight; as stated by al-Shumunni and al-Birjandi and others among the authors of commentaries and fatwas. If it is said: It should be that salam in measured items is not permissible because salam is established contrary to analogy as it is sale of a non-existent, and the text came regarding measured-by-volume (kayli) and measured-by-weight (wazni). We reply: Measured items are annexed to them by textual indication because His statement: 'So let him give salaf in a known volume and a known weight' necessitated permissibility in volumetrics and weightables because of the possibility of equivalence in delivery as described in the salaf item, and equivalence as achieved by volume is also achieved by measure (dhirā'), so salam in measured items is valid by way of indication, as in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the commentary on al-Hidayah. The passage explains the permissibility of salam (advance sale) in measured items (al-madhru'at) such as cloth, provided that length, width, thickness, and coarseness are specified. The author notes a difference of opinion: Ibn Aban's view (that the contract is valid) is considered more correct. Abu Bakr al-A'mash had a contrary view. The dispute applies when salam is given in something other than gold or silver; if one pays gold for silver or vice versa, it is invalid by consensus due to riba al-nasa'. Regarding copper coins (fulus), the Hanafi school has two views: the prevailing narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permits salam in fulus by number; Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The passage defends the analogy allowing salam in measured items based on textual indication (dalālah): the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:282) mentioning known volume and weight establishes the principle of equivalence, which is also achievable through measurement (dhirā'). Thus salam in measured items is valid. For silk, weight must also be mentioned because value varies by weight. This is a classical example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) and istihsan.

Key Terms
المذروع (al-madhru'): An item sold by linear measure (dhirā') such as cloth, fabric.
الفلوس (al-fulus): Copper coins used as currency but not created for that purpose; considered non-monetary according to this passage.
التسوية (al-taswiyah): Equivalence or precise matching between what is described and what is delivered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam in measured items (like cloth) considered valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Quran explicitly mentions measurement (dhirā')
B) Because equivalence in delivery can be achieved by measurement just as with volume and weight
C) Because silk requires mentioning weight
D) Because the text allows salam in any known commodity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates salam in measured items by extending the Quran's permission via qiyas khafi based on the shared illah of equivalence in delivery.

Salam in Counted Items (Al-Ma'dud al-Mutaqarib)
Specifies conditions for salam in counted items that are similar and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute via custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid salam in counted items and apply the custom-based resolution of the ostrich eggs dispute.

Core Idea
Salam in counted items is valid only if each unit is similar in value; custom may determine the ruling.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on salam (forward sale) for counted items. The passage clarifies that only items with uniform individual value (mutaqarib) qualify, while those with wide variation (mutafawit) do not. A key dispute on ostrich eggs shows how custom ('urf) can resolve scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is salam in counted items. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) under the condition that the items are mutaqarib (similar in individual value).
The author lists examples: walnuts, eggs, copper coins, milk, bricks.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'falyusallim fi kaylin ma'lum wa waznin ma'lum' (give salam in known volume and weight). This is extended to counted and measured items by dalaalah (textual indication) because the underlying reason is the possibility of equivalence in delivery.
The passage cites al-Kifayah for this extension.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith's mention of volume and weight shows that the key condition is known quantity and ability to deliver equivalence. Counted items with similar individual value also allow equivalence, so the ruling is analogously applied.
Equivalence (taswiyah) is achieved by number for mutaqarib items.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
On ostrich eggs, the apparent narration (Abu Hanifa) considers them mutaqarib, but a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad prohibits salam by number due to variation. The author reconciles by looking at custom and purpose.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Apply the custom-based resolution
If the custom is to use the eggs for eating (uniformity), the first view applies; if for shells (where size and colour matter), the second view applies and further specifications (quantity, colour) are required.
This shows how 'urf determines operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعدود متقارباً : كالجوز، والبيض، والفلس، واللبن، والآجر والمعدود متقارباً : كالجوز، والبيض، والفلس، واللبن، والآجر قلنا : يلحق المذروعات بهما بدلالة النص لِمَا أنَّ قولَه : «فليسلم في كـيـل معلوم ووزن معلوم»، إنما اقتضى الجواز في المكيل والموزون باعتبار إمكان التسوية في التسليم على ما وصف في المسلم فيه والتسوية كما يتحقق بالكيل كذلك يتحقق بالذرع ، فيجوزُ السَّلَمَ في المذروعات بطريقِ الدلالة، كذا في «الكفاية»). (1) قوله : والمعدود...الخ ؛ وإنما صح السَّلَمُ في المعدود المتقارب ؛ لأنه معلوم القدر محفوظ الوصف، مقدورُ التسليم، والمراد بالمتقارب ما لا يكون بين آحاده تفاوت في القيمة، ويضمنُ بالمثل كالجوز والبيض وغيرهما مما عده المصنف .
وأما المتفاوت بين آحادها بالصغرِ والكبرِ فساقط الاعتبار فيما بين النَّاسِ، وقيد بالمتقارب ؛ لأن المتفاوت كالبطيخ والرُّمانِ والسفرجل لا يصح السَّلَمُ فيه عدداً لتفاوتِ
آحاده في القيمة. والجوز ثمر معروف معرَّب كوز جمعه : جوزات، كذا في «القاموس»(۲) ، والمراد الجــوز الشامي والفرنجي ؛ لعدم التفاوت فيه، لا الجوز الهندي، كذا في
«البحر» (۳).
والبيض: تخمهاي مرغ، جمع بيضة. كذا في «المنتخب»، ظاهرُ الروايةِ أنَّ بيض النَّعام من المتقارب، وفي رواية الحسن عن الإمام الله : لا يجوز لتفاوتِ آحاده ، والوجه أن ينظر إلى الغرض من العرف، فإن كان الغرض منه الأكل فقط ، كعرف أهل البوادي ، وجب العمل بالرواية الأولى. وإن كان الغرض منه القشر للاتِّخاذ في سلاسل القناديل، كما هو شائع في مصر وغيرها من البلاد، وجب العمل بالرواية الثانية، ووجب مع ذكر العدد تعيين المقدار واللون من نقاء البياض وإهداره، صرح به في الفتح القدير».
And counted items that are similar: such as walnuts, eggs, copper coins, milk, and bricks. And counted items that are similar: such as walnuts, eggs, copper coins, milk, and bricks. We said: measured items are annexed to them by textual indication because His statement: 'So let him give salaf in a known volume and a known weight' necessitated permissibility in volumetrics and weightables because of the possibility of equivalence in delivery as described in the salaf item, and equivalence as achieved by volume is also achieved by measure, so salam in measured items is valid by way of indication, as in al-Kifayah. (1) His statement: 'and counted items...' etc. Salam is valid in counted items that are similar because they are known in quantity, preserved in description, capable of delivery. And what is meant by 'similar' (mutaqarib) is that there is no difference in value among its individual units, and it is guaranteed by like, such as walnuts, eggs, and others that the author listed. As for items whose individual units differ in smallness and largeness, they are of no consideration among people. The restriction to 'similar' is because dissimilar items like watermelon, pomegranate, and quince are not valid for salam by number due to variation in value. Walnut is a well-known fruit, arabicized from Persian 'gawz', its plural is jawzāt, as in al-Qamus. What is meant is Syrian and European walnuts, because there is no variation in them, not Indian walnuts, as in al-Bahr. Eggs: [Persian] 'tukhm-i-murgh', plural of baydah. As in al-Muntakhab. The apparent narration is that ostrich eggs are among similar items. In a narration of al-Hasan from Imam (Abu Hanifa), it is not permissible due to variation in size. The correct view is to look at the custom-based purpose: if the purpose is only eating, as is the custom of Bedouins, then the first narration is followed. If the purpose is the shell for use in chains of lanterns, as is common in Egypt and other countries, then the second narration is followed, and it is necessary to specify the quantity and colour (whiteness or otherwise) along with the number, as stated in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of salam in counted items (al-ma'dud). The ruling states that salam is valid in counted items that are 'mutaqarib' (similar/close in individual value), such as walnuts, eggs, copper coins, milk, bricks. The reason is that the quantity is known, description preserved, and delivery possible. Items that differ significantly in size/value (like watermelons, pomegranates) are not eligible for salam by number. A key point: walnuts must be of the uniform type (Syrian or European), not Indian walnuts which vary. Regarding eggs, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about ostrich eggs: the apparent narration (Abu Hanifa) considers them similar and thus valid; in a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad, they are not due to variation. The author resolves this by looking at customary purpose: if used only for eating, the first view applies; if used for their shells (as in lanterns), then the second view applies, requiring specification of quantity, colour, and clarity. This shows how 'urf (custom) and maqsad (purpose) can determine the operative ruling in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
المعدود المتقارب (al-ma'dud al-mutaqarib): Counted items whose individual units are similar in value and insured by like.
المتفاوت (al-mutafawit): Items whose individual units differ significantly in size/value such that salam by number is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for salam in counted items according to this passage?
A) The items must be measured by volume.
B) The items must be uniform in individual value (mutaqarib).
C) The items must be perishable.
D) The items must be imported.

Key Takeaway
Salam in counted items is valid only if the units are similar in value; custom determines the resolution of disputes.

Salam in Countable Similar Items and Measured Items by Implication
Expands ruling on salam in countable and measured items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for salam in countable similar items and apply dalalat al-nass to derive the ruling for measured items by length.

Core Idea
Salam is valid when items can be delivered uniformly, whether by count, weight, volume, or length.

The Hanafi school expands salam beyond weighed and measured items to include similar countable items and items sold by length. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning (dalalat al-nass) and the crucial condition of value similarity (mutaqarib). We also explore a practical intra-madhhab difference on ostrich eggs, resolved by custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of salam items in the passage
The author discusses countable similar items (al-ma'dud al-mutaqarib) and measured items by length (al-madhrurat). Note the examples given for each.
Countable similar items include walnuts and eggs; measured items include cloth.
2
Understand the condition of similarity (mutaqarib)
Salam by number is valid only when the individual units do not differ significantly in value. The passage explains that items like watermelons and pomegranates are excluded due to natural variation.
This condition is based on the guarantee of delivery (tamathul).
3
Trace the legal extension to measured items (dalalat al-nass)
The hadith mentions salam in known measure (kayl) and known weight (wazn). The effective cause (illa) is the possibility of equal delivery (taswiyah). Since equality is also achieved by linear measurement (dhar'), salam in such items is permissible by implication of the text.
This is an example of Hanafi dalalat al-nass, distinct from explicit qiyas.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ostrich eggs
The passage presents two narrations: one deeming ostrich eggs similar (valid), another deeming them dissimilar. The resolution depends on the customary purpose—eating versus decorative use.
This shows how custom (urf) can determine the operative ruling.
5
Extract the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view follows custom: if the purpose is consumption, treat as similar; if decorative, require additional specifications (quantity, color). This is consistent with Hanafi flexibility.
Authority weight shifts from Zahir al-Riwayah to Nawadir based on context.

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling of salam in countable items. The author clarifies that salam is valid in countable items that are similar in value, where there is no significant disparity (e.g., walnuts, eggs). The term 'similar' is defined by the lack of variation in price among individual units. Items like watermelon or pomegranate are excluded due to natural variation. The passage also extends the ruling to measured items (by length, e.g., cloth) through textual implication: the hadith mentioning 'known measure' and 'known weight' implies that any method ensuring uniform delivery (including measurement by length) suffices. Additionally, the passage discusses a specific case of ostrich eggs, noting two narrations: one deeming them similar (suitable for salam by count), another not (due to size variation). The resolution depends on the customary purpose—if for consumption, similar rulings apply; if for decorative use, the second narration is followed, requiring specification of quantity and color.

Key Terms
المعدود المتقارب (al-ma'dud al-mutaqarib): Countable items whose individual units are similar in value, with no significant disparity, making them suitable for salam by number.
المذروعات (al-madhrurat): Items sold by linear measurement (dhar'), such as cloth, allowed in salam by implication of the text.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): Textual implication: deriving a ruling for an unmentioned case from the underlying reason (illa) of a mentioned case.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Salam in Fils (Copper Coins)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in fils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on salam in fils and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
Salam in fils is allowed because parties can treat copper coins as commodities by convention.

The permissibility of salam in fils (copper coins) is a point of intra-Hanafi disagreement. This passage from Umdat al-Ri'aya presents the views of the founding imams, anchored in the principle that thamaniyya (monetary nature) is subject to the contracting parties' convention. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school treats fiduciary currencies in muamalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the three positions
The passage discusses salam (advance sale) in fils. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it permissible; Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it invalid.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.
2
Analyze the basis for permissibility
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that the monetary nature (thamaniyya) of fils is conventional. The parties can void it by agreement, turning fils into a specified commodity (mutamawwal), making salam valid.
Thamaniyya is not inherent in fils.
3
Analyze Muhammad's objection
Muhammad argues that fils are inherently currencies (athman), like dirhams and dinars. Salam in currencies is prohibited by consensus, so salam in fils is also invalid.
He analogizes fils to gold and silver coins.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The author notes that al-Jami' al-Saghir mentions permissibility absolutely, indicating the prevailing view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
5
Apply to similar cases
Extend the principle to modern fiduciary currencies (e.g., paper money) where the parties' convention can affect their status as commodities or currency.
Later Hanafis treat modern fiat money similarly to fils.

As for the fils: its permissibility in salam is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir absolutely without any disagreement. It is said: its permissibility is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the monetary nature (thamaniyya) with respect to the contracting parties is by their convention, so it is voided by their convention. When it is voided, it becomes a commodity (mutamawwal) specified by identification, so salam is valid in it. According to Muhammad, it is not valid because fils are currency (athman) and salam is not valid in currencies by consensus, just as if one gave salam in dirhams and dinars, it is not valid, so too here. But if it is unspecific, it must be known and marked, as in al-Jawhara, by mentioning its width, length, and thickness. (2) His statement: 'it is not said... etc.': al-Azhari said: If salt is abundant, you say 'mallaḥahā tamlīḥan', and fish is milḥ, mamlūḥ, and malīḥ, which is the estimated, and it is not said 'māliḥ' except in a weak language. And water became salty 'mulūḥa', this is the language of the people of al-Aliya, and the agent from it is 'miliḥ' with fatḥa on mīm and kasra on lām, like 'khushuna' becomes 'khushūna' so it is 'khushun', this is the origin for the active participle. With it, Talha ibn Musarrif recited 'and this is bitter water' (Surah al-Furqan: 53), but when its usage became frequent, it was lightened, and usage limited to it, so it was said 'milḥ' with kasra on mīm and sukūn on lām. And the people...

Commentary
This passage covers three rulings: (1) Salam is valid in salted fish; the linguistic note clarifies that 'salted' is properly 'mamlūḥ' or 'malīḥ', not 'māliḥ' in standard usage. (2) The main dispute is on salam in fils (copper coins). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule it permissible because the parties can agree to treat fils as a commodity by convention, overriding their default status as currency. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, arguing that fils are inherently currencies (athman) like dirhams and dinars, and salam in currencies is prohibited by consensus. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as found in al-Jami' al-Saghir without mention of disagreement. (3) For salam in milk, if the milk is specified (mu'ayyan), no further description of its thickness, width, or place of production is needed; if unspecified, these must be mentioned for clarity. The linguistic note on 'malīḥ' is from al-Misbah al-Munir and al-Azhari, referencing Quranic usage.

Key Terms
الفلس (al-fals (plural: fulus)): Copper coin used as currency but can be treated as a commodity by convention.
الثمنية (al-thamaniyya): The quality of being a price or currency medium; monetary nature.

Salam in Fulus: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in fulus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding salam in fulus and distinguish the proofs of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf from that of Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Fulus can become commodities by party agreement; their price-character is conventional, not fixed.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over whether salam (advance payment sale) is valid for copper coins (fulus). The disagreement turns on a subtle question: is the 'price-character' (thumaniyyah) of fulus a fixed property, or can it be changed by the mutual agreement of the contracting parties? Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles of stipulation and custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its authority
First, note that the text opens by stating that al-Jami' al-Saghir mentions permissibility of salam in fulus absolutely, without recording any disagreement. This gives you an initial sense of the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is a Zahir al-Riwayah text by Imam Muhammad himself, making its ruling authoritative.
2
Extract the Hanafi majority position (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
Identify the reasoning: thumaniyyah is by mutual agreement, so the parties can nullify it, turning fulus into a commodity (muthamman). Consequently, salam becomes permissible.
Key phrase: 'al-thumaniyyah fi haqq al-muta'aqidayni bi-istilahihima'
3
Extract the dissenting position (Imam Muhammad)
Muhammad argues that fulus are inherently prices (athman), and salam in prices is prohibited by consensus. He draws a qiyas (analogy) to dirhams and dinars, where salam is invalid.
This disagreement is an ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
4
Analyse the point of contention (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, one can give salam in fulus (e.g., pay 1000 fulus now to receive 1200 fulus later). Under Muhammad, such a contract would be invalid.
The dispute hinges on whether fulus are considered prices by nature or by convention.
5
Determine the operative position for fatwa
The text indicates that the permissibility view is recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir, which is a primary source, and is likely the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position. Later Hanafi works generally adopt this view.
This is a case where the majority of the school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) outweigh the single dissenting imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفلس: فجواز السلم فيه مذكور في الجامع الصغير مطلقاً من غير ذكر خلاف لأحد وقيل : جوازه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف الله ؛ لأن الثمنية في حق المتعاقدين باصطلاحهما، فتبطل باصطلاحهما ، وإذا بطلت صار مثمناً يتعين بالتعين ، فجاز السلم فيه. وعند محمد ه لا يجوز؛ لأنَّ الفلوس أثمان، ولا يجوز السلم في الأثمان بالإجماع كما إذا أسلم في الدراهم والدنانير فلا يجوز، فكذا هاهنا.
As for the fils (copper coin): the permissibility of salam in it is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir absolutely without any mention of disagreement. And it is said: its permissibility is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because the quality of being a price (thumaniyyah) is by mutual agreement of the contracting parties, so it can be rendered void by their agreement. When it is voided, it becomes a commodity (muthamman) that becomes specified by specification, so salam in it is permissible. According to Muhammad, it is not permissible, because fils are prices, and salam in prices is not permissible by consensus, just as if one gives salam in dirhams and dinars, it is not permissible, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of salam (advance payment sale) in fulus (copper coins). The text first notes that in al-Jami' al-Saghir, the permissibility is mentioned without recording any disagreement. Then a different view is reported: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit salam in fulus. Their reasoning is that the status of being a price (thumaniyyah) is determined by the mutual agreement of the parties. Since they can agree to treat fulus as a commodity (muthamman) by specifying them individually, the bar on salam in prices no longer applies. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that fulus are inherently prices (athman), and salam in prices is prohibited by consensus, analogous to dirhams and dinars. This is a clear example of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, where the difference hinges on whether the price-commodity nature of fulus is fixed or subject to party stipulation.

Key Terms
الفلس (al-fals (pl. fulus)): Copper coin used as currency; its status as price or commodity is debated.
الثمنية (al-thumaniyyah): The quality or status of being a price (thaman).
السلم (al-salam): Advance payment sale: paying in full for goods to be delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit salam in fulus?
A) Because fulus are not really prices.
B) Because the parties can agree to treat them as commodities.
C) Because the prohibition on salam in prices only applies to gold and silver.
D) Because fulus are considered foodstuffs.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of salam in fulus depends on whether their price-character is fixed (Muhammad's view) or subject to party stipulation (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view, which is the mufta bihi).

Salam in Specific Milk: No Additional Description Needed
Ruling on the requirement to describe milk in salam when it is specific.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for describing milk in a salam contract when the milk is specific versus non-specific, and apply the distinction to classify salam transactions as sahih or requiring additional description.

Core Idea
In salam, specific milk needs no description; non-specific milk must be described by dimensions.

In a salam contract, the subject matter must be known to avoid uncertainty (gharar). This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a specific case: milk. If the milk is individually identified (mu'ayyan), such as from a particular animal, no further description is needed. But if the milk is unspecified, the seller must define it by mentioning its width, length, and thickness to make it sufficiently known.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and identify the two cases: specific milk (mu'ayyan) and non-specific milk (ghayr mu'ayyan).
The text contrasts 'idha kana mu'ayyinan' with 'idha kana ghayr mu'ayyan'.
2
State the ruling for each
For specific milk: no need to describe its quality or place of origin. For non-specific milk: must be described by dimensions (width, length, thickness).
The ruling for non-specific milk is derived from al-Jawhara.
3
Understand the rationale
The principle behind salam is that the object must be known to eliminate gharar. Specificity satisfies this; otherwise, description is needed.
This aligns with the general Hanafi requirement that salam subject matter be ma'lum (known).
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario, determine whether the milk is specific or not, then state whether additional description is required for a valid salam.
For example, milk from a named cow is specific; milk from an undefined source is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : بملبن معين ؛ ولا حاجة إلى قيدِهِ ببيان صفته ومكان ضربه ، كما وقع في «التنوير»؛ لأنَّ اللبن إذا كان معيّناً لم يحتج إلى ذلك البيان، أما إذا كان غير معين فلا بد من كونه معلوماً ومعلّم، كما في «الجوهرة» بذكر عرضه وطوله وسمكه.
His statement: 'with specific milk' — and there is no need to restrict it by stating its description and place of origin, as occurred in al-Tanwir, because when the milk is specific, it does not need that statement. As for when it is not specific, it must be known and marked, as in al-Jawhara, by mentioning its width, length, and thickness.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This short passage is a ruling on the conditions for salam in milk. The matn says 'with specific milk' (bimalabin mu'ayyan). The commentator clarifies that if the milk is individually identified (mu'ayyan), there is no need to describe its quality or the place where it was milked. However, if the milk is unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan), it must be defined by mentioning its dimensions (breadth, length, thickness) to avoid uncertainty. This follows the general principle that salam requires the subject matter to be known (ma'lum) to prevent gharar. The reference to al-Tanwir and al-Jawhara indicates that this is an established position in the later Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
اللبن المعين (al-laban al-mu'ayyan): Milk that is specifically identified (e.g., the milk of a particular animal or container).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the milk is from a known breed of animal.
B) When the milk is specifically identified (mu'ayyan).
C) When the milk is from a particular region.
D) When the milk is fresh.

Key Takeaway
Specific milk in salam needs no description; non-specific milk must be described by dimensions to prevent gharar.

Salam in Salted Fish: Ruling and Linguistic Clarification
Ruling with linguistic expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in salted fish and evaluate the linguistic defense of the term 'malih' as a valid Arabic word.

Core Idea
Salam in salted fish is valid; the term 'malih' is legitimate Hijazi Arabic, so linguistic objections do not invalidate the contract.

The Hanafi position on salam (advance sale) in salted fish is straightforward: it is permissible as long as the subject matter is well-defined. However, the commentary delves into a linguistic debate about the word 'malih', which some claim is incorrect Arabic. Understanding this debate strengthens one's appreciation of how Hanafi scholars rely on authoritative language usage to support legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the statement 'فصح في السمك المليح' which directly states the validity of salam in salted fish. This is the matn (base text).
2
Understand the subject matter
The commentary clarifies that 'السمك المليح' means fish preserved with salt (القديد بالملح). Recognize that the definition is broad enough to cover various salted fish.
3
Analyze the linguistic objection
Some claim that 'مالح' (malih) is a weak or incorrect term, preferring 'مليح' or 'مملوح'. The commentary cites multiple authorities to defend 'مالح' as a valid Hijazi dialect.
4
Evaluate the commentator's defense
The commentator argues that 'مالح' is a legitimate word used by the eloquent Arabs of Hijaz, and its rarity is only due to irregular morphological derivation, not lack of authenticity.
The Quran itself uses words from Hijazi dialect, supporting its authority.
5
Conclude the ruling's applicability
Since the term is linguistically sound, the ruling of validity stands. The linguistic objection does not affect the fiqh ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The ruling itself is straightforward: the permissibility of salam in salted fish is established.

مليح (malih): Salted fish preserved with salt; the word is argued to be a valid Arabic term despite some objections.

Salam in Fresh Fish: The Seasonality Condition
Ruling on salam in fresh fish conditional on season

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of salam in fresh fish and apply it to seasonal and geographical scenarios.

Core Idea
Salam in fresh fish is valid only when delivery falls within the fish's natural season.

Salam (advance payment) for fresh fish carries a risk of gharar because fish may become unavailable before delivery. The Hanafi school therefore requires that the delivery term be set within the period when the fish is naturally present in water. This lesson examines the ruling and its practical application across seasons and regions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that salam in fresh fish (samak tari) is being ruled upon. The ruling: it is permissible only when the delivery term coincides with the fish's season (hin).
The act is a salam contract, a type of forward sale.
2
Pinpoint the core condition
The condition is that the fish must be available in water at the time of delivery. This avoids uncertainty (gharar) about the subject matter's existence.
‘La yajuz illa fi hin yujad al-samak fi al-ma’ – not permissible except when fish exists in water.
3
Apply to seasonal variation
If fish disappears in winter (e.g., due to freezing), salam cannot be made in winter. If made in summer, the delivery term must not extend into winter.
‘In kan yanqati' fi ba'd al-sana… la yan'aqid fi al-shita'.
4
Note the geographical exception
In places where fish is available year‑round (no seasonal disappearance), the contract is valid at any time because the condition is automatically met.
‘Wa in kana fi balad la yanqati'…’
5
Consequence of violation
If the term extends into a period of non‑availability, the contract is invalid (la yan'aqid). There is no need for rescission; it is void ab initio.
The invalidity stems from inability to deliver the specified subject matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطري في حينه فقط : أي السَّلَمُ في السَّمَكِ الطَّري لا يجوز إلا في حين يوجد السَّمَك في الماء. قوله : لا يجوز إلا في حين يوجد...الخ ؛ فإن كان ينقطع في بعض السنة كما ينقطعُ في الشتاء في بعض البلادِ لانجمادِ الماء فلا ينعقد في الشتاء، ولو أسلم في الصيف وجب أن يكون الأجل لا يبلغ الشتاء. وهذا معنى قول محمد الله : لا خير في السمك الطري إلا في حينه : يعني أن يكون السَّلَمُ مع شروطه في حينه كيلا ينقطع بعد العقدِ والحلول، وإن كان في بلد لا ينقطع.
And the fresh (fish) only in its season: i.e., salam in fresh fish is not permissible except in the time when fish exist in water. His statement: 'not permissible except in the time when it exists...' For if it becomes unavailable in some part of the year, as it becomes unavailable in winter in some places due to freezing of water, then it is not concluded in winter. And if one gives salam in summer, the term must not reach winter. This is the meaning of Muhammad's statement: 'There is no good in fresh fish except in its season,' meaning that salam must be with its conditions in its season so that it does not become unavailable after the contract and before delivery, unless it is in a place where it does not become unavailable.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on salam in fresh fish (samak tari). The condition is that the delivery period must fall within the time when the fish is naturally available in water. If the fish will be unavailable during the term (e.g., due to winter freezing), the contract is invalid if the term extends into that period. For example, if salam is conducted in summer, the delivery term must end before winter when fish might disappear. This ensures that the subject matter is deliverable at the stipulated time, avoiding gharar. Imam Muhammad is quoted as saying there is no good in fresh fish except in its season, meaning the contract must be timed appropriately. An exception is made for places where fish is available year-round.

Key Terms
السمك الطري (al-samak al-tari): Fresh fish (as opposed to salted fish).
الحينه (al-hin): The time when the fish is naturally available in water; its season.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At any time of the year.
B) Only during the summer when fish are plentiful.
C) Only when the delivery period falls within the fish's natural season.
D) Only if the fish is caught on the day of the contract.

Key Takeaway
Salam in fresh fish is valid only when the delivery term is set within the fish's natural season of availability.

Salam in Fresh Fish and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Animals
Ruling with proof and madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for salam in fresh fish and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i position on salam in animals.

Core Idea
Salam in fresh fish is valid only in its season; large fish meat follows the ruling of meat, not fish.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya combines a nuanced fiqh ruling on salam in fresh fish with a linguistic defense of the word 'malih' and a cross-madhhab comparison. The Hanafi school imposes strict conditions to avoid gharar, while al-Shafi'i permits salam in animals absolutely. Understanding the conditions and the basis of the ikhtilaf is essential for proper application of salam contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on salam in fresh fish
Locate the key condition: the fish must be available (in its season) for the entire term of the contract. If the fish disappears (e.g., due to winter freezing), the contract is invalid.
The phrase 'في حين يوجد السمك في الماء' is the basis.
2
Distinguish between large and small fish
Large fish require known weight and type; small fish require only known weight. This distinction arises from the analogy with meat for large fish.
See the reference to al-Hidayah and Abu Hanifa's position.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection on salam in animals
Al-Shafi'i permits salam in animals absolutely, arguing that specification of type and description removes uncertainty. The Hanafi school holds that the unknown quantity of meat (due to bones and variable cuts) still constitutes gharar.
This is the core of the inter-madhhab dispute.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi does not permit salam in animals or large fish meat; Shafi'i permits both. For fresh fish, both schools likely agree if conditions are met, but Hanafi restricts by season.
The thamarah directly affects contract drafting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطري في حينه (فقط) : أي السَّلَمُ في السَّمَكِ الطَّري لا يجوز إلا في حين يوجد السَّمَك في الماء. الحجاز يقولون : أَمْلَحَ الماءُ إِمْلاحاً ، والفاعل : مالِح من النوادر التي جاءت على غير قياس نحو : أبقل الموضعُ [فهو باقل، وأغضى الليلُ فهو غاض، وأنشد ابن فارس له : وماء قوم مالح ونافع ونقله أيضاً عن ابن الأَعْرَابي، وأنشد بعضُهم لعمرو بن أبي ربيعة : لأصبح ماء البحر من ريقها عذبا فلو تفلت في البحر والبحر مالح ونقل الأَزْهَرِيُّ : اختلاف الناس في جواز مالح، ثم قال : ماء مالح وملح أيضاً، وفي نسخة من «التهذيب : قلت : مالح : لغة لا تنكر وإن كانت قليلة. وقال في «المجرد» : ماء مالح وملح ،بمعنى، وعبارة المتقدمين فيه، ومالح قليل، ويعنون بقلتِه كونه لم يجيء على فِعْلِهِ، فلم يهتد بعض المتأخرين إلى مفادهم، وحملوا القلة . على الشهرة والثبوت، وليس كذلك. بل هي محمولة على جريانِهِ على فِعْلِه ، وقد نُقِلَ أَنَّها لغةٌ حجازية، وصرَّحَ أهلُ اللغة بأنَّ أهل الحجاز كانوا يختارون من اللغاتِ أفصحها ومن الألفاظ أعــذبها فيستعملونه ؛ ولهذا نَزَلَ القرآن بلغتهم، وكان منهم أفصح العرب، وما ثبت أنه من لغتهم لا يجوز القولُ بعدم فصاحته. انتهى. بأدنى اختصار. وقد عرفت من هذه العبارة أن المالح من لغة أهل الحجاز، ويستعملونه في محاوراتهم، وليس المقصود من قِلَّتِهِ قلَّةُ الشهرة والثبوت، فقول الشارح : لا يقال : مالح إلا في لغة رديئة ؛ ليس مما أحصله.
[١] قوله : لا يجوز إلا في حين يوجد...الخ ؛ فإن كان ينقطع في بعض السنة كما ينقطعُ في الشتاء في بعض البلادِ لانجمادِ الماء فلا ينعقد في الشتاء، ولو أسلم في الصيف وجب أن يكون الأجل لا يبلغ الشتاء. وهذا معنى قول محمد الله : لا خير في السمك الطري إلا في حينه : يعني أن يكون السَّلَمُ مع شروطه في حينه كيلا ينقطع بعد العقدِ والحلول، وإن كان في بلد لا ينقطع.
وزناً وضرباً معلومين : أي لا بُدَّ أن يُذكر وزن معلوم، ونوع معلوم، والطَّسْتُ) ، والقُمْقُمةُ ) ، والخفِّين) إلا إذا لم يعرف به ) : أي بالصفة. إلا فيما لا يُعْلَمُ قَدْرُهُ وصفتُهُ كالحيوان) ، وعند الشافعي (۲۳۳) له يجوز جاز مطلقاً. فأما المليح فإنه يدَّخرُ ويباع في الأسواق فلا ينقطع حتى لو كان ينقطع في بعض الأحيان لا يجوز ، كما صرَّحَ به العلامة الشامي)، وغيره. وزناً وضرباً معلومين: هذا في كبار السمك ، وأمَّا الصغار منه فالسَلَمُ جائز فيه وزناً معلوماً طرياً كان أو مليحاً، ذكره البرْجَنْدِي، وعن أبي حنيفة له : إنه لا يجوز في لحم الكبار منها، وهي التي تقطع اعتباراً بالسَلَم في اللحم عنده، كذا في «الهداية). [ ١ ] قوله : القمقمة : كقنفذة كماسه، كذا في منتهى الأرب»، وكذا في «الصراح»، وفي «البرهان القاطع»: كماسه کاسه جوبین باشد. انتهی. وقال في «المصباح المنير»: «القُمْقُم : آنية العطار، والقُمْتُمُ أيضاً آنية من نحاس يُسَخَّنُ فيها الماء، وأهل الشام يقولونه : غلاية ، والقُمْقُم : رومي معرَّب، وقد يؤنَّثُ بالهاء، فيقال : قُمْقُمة، وعاء من صفر، يستصحبه المسافر ، والجمعُ القماقم». انتهى [٢) قوله : والخفين؛ بأن يقال للخفاف: أحرز لي من أديمك خفا يوافق رجلي بكذا، ويريه رجله.
[٣]قوله : وعند الشافعي ... الخ ; حاصله أنَّ السَّلَمَ في الحيوان يجوزُ عنده ؛ لأنَّ الحيوان يصير معلوماً إذا بين جنسه كالإبل ونحوه، ونوعه كالبختي والعربي، ووصفه
And fresh (fish) in its season (only): meaning salam in fresh fish is only permissible when the fish exists in the water. The people of Hijaz say: 'amlah al-ma'u imlahan' (the water became salty), and the active participle is 'malih', one of the rare forms that come not according to analogy, like: 'abqala al-mawdu'u fahuwa baqil' (the land produced herbage, so it is baqil), and 'aghda al-laylu fahuwa ghad' (the night became dark, so it is ghad). Ibn Faris recited for him: 'And the water of a people is malih and beneficial.' And he also transmitted from Ibn al-A'rabi, and some recited for 'Amr ibn Abi Rabi'ah: 'Then the sea water would become sweet from her saliva, so if she spat in the sea, and the sea is malih.' And al-Azhari transmitted the difference of people regarding the permissibility of 'malih', then he said: 'Water malih and milh also.' And in a copy of al-Tahdhib: 'I said: malih is a language not denied, though it is rare.' And he said in al-Mujarrad: 'Water malih and milh are synonymous.' The statement of the earlier scholars about it, 'malih is rare,' means by its rarity that it did not come upon its verb. So some later scholars did not understand their import and interpreted rarity as lack of fame and establishedness, but that is not so. Rather it is interpreted as its non-conformity to its verb. And it has been transmitted that it is a Hijazi dialect. The language scholars stated that the Hijazis used to choose the most eloquent of languages and the sweetest of words and use them; hence the Quran was revealed in their language, and among them were the most eloquent of Arabs. And what is established as part of their language cannot be said to be non-eloquent. End, with slight abridgment. And you have known from this statement that 'malih' is from the language of the Hijazis and they use it in their conversations, and the intended meaning of its rarity is not lack of fame and establishment, so the commentator's saying: 'malih is not said except in a poor language' is not what I have concluded.
[1] His saying: 'is not permissible except when it exists...' etc.; if [the fish] becomes unavailable in some part of the year, as it becomes unavailable in winter in some countries due to freezing of water, then [the contract] does not take effect in winter. If one makes a salam contract in summer, the term must not reach winter. This is the meaning of Muhammad's saying: 'There is no good in fresh fish except in its season,' meaning that the salam with its conditions should be in its season so that it does not become unavailable after contract and maturity. And if it is in a country where it is not unavailable.
By known weight and type: meaning it is necessary to mention a known weight and a known type. And the tasht (basin) and the qumquma (flask) and the khuffayn (boots) except when it is not known thereby (i.e., by description). Except for what is not known in quantity and description, like animals. And according to al-Shafi'i (233) it is permissible absolutely. As for the salted [fish], it is stored and sold in markets, so it is not unavailable; even if it becomes unavailable at times, it is not permissible, as explicitly stated by 'Allama al-Shami and others. 'By known weight and type': this applies to large fish. As for small ones, salam is permissible in them by known weight, whether fresh or salted, as mentioned by al-Barjandi. And from Abu Hanifa: it is not permissible in the meat of large ones, which are cut, by analogy with salam in meat according to him, as in al-Hidayah. [1] His saying: 'al-qumquma': like qanfudha (hedgehog) in form. As in Muntaha al-Arab and al-Sirah. And in al-Burhan al-Qati': it is a vessel. End. And he said in al-Misbah al-Munir: 'al-qumqum is the perfumer's vessel, and also a copper vessel in which water is heated; the people of Syria call it ghilaya. Al-qumqum is a Romanized word, and may be feminine with the feminine ending, so it is said qumquma, a brass vessel carried by a traveler; its plural is qamaqim.' End. [2] His saying: 'and the khuffayn': such that one says to the bootmaker: 'Make me a boot from your leather that fits my foot for such-and-such price,' and he shows him his foot.
[3] His saying: 'And according to al-Shafi'i...' etc.; its summary is that salam in animals is permissible according to him, because the animal becomes known when its type is specified, like camels and the like, and its species, like Bikhti and Arabi, and its description.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of salam (forward sale) in fresh fish, along with a linguistic discussion on the word 'malih' and a comparison with the Shafi'i school regarding salam in animals. The commentator first explains that salam in fresh fish is only valid when the fish is available (في حينه). He then digresses into a detailed linguistic analysis defending the word 'malih' (salty) as a valid Hijazi dialect, countering the claim that it is a poor language. He cites various authorities to show that even though 'malih' is irregular in form, it is eloquent due to its Hijazi origin. Returning to the main topic, the commentator elaborates on the condition that the fish must be available throughout the term of the contract; if it disappears seasonally (e.g., due to freezing in winter), the contract is invalid if the term extends into that season. The text then discusses the requirements for salam in fish: known weight and type. For large fish, weight and type must be specified; for small fish, weight alone suffices. The commentator also mentions Salam in utensils like tasht (basin) and qumquma (flask) and khuffayn (boots) when their description suffices. He notes the Shafi'i position that salam in animals is permissible absolutely, whereas the Hanafi position (according to Abu Hanifa) does not permit it in the meat of large fish by analogy with meat, as recorded in al-Hidayah. The passage thus combines a ruling, a linguistic note, and an inter-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
السَّلَمُ (al-salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for a specified commodity to be delivered later.
طري (tariy): Fresh (fish), as opposed to salted or dried.
مالح (malih): An adjective meaning 'salty', used for water or fish; considered a valid Hijazi dialect form.
قُمْقُمة (qumquma): A brass vessel for water or perfume, often carried by travelers.
الخفّين (al-khuffayn): Leather boots; salam in custom-made boots is permissible if description suffices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically forbade it.

Key Takeaway
Salam in fresh fish requires the fish to be available throughout the contract term; large fish meat is treated like meat and thus invalid in Hanafi, while small fish are permissible by weight alone.

Salam in Fish: Conditions of Weight and Type
States ruling on salam in fish and containers with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid salam contract in fish and distinguish the Hanafi rulings for large vs. small fish, including the intra-school difference on cut fish.

Core Idea
Salam in fish is valid if weight and type are known; large cut fish follow meat rules per Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi text on salam contracts, focusing on fish. The passage clarifies that both weight and type must be specified for large fish, while small fish require only weight. Additionally, it introduces an intra-Hanafi difference regarding large fish cut into pieces, analogized to salam in meat, which Abu Hanifa does not allow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and general conditions
Recall that salam is an advance payment sale where the price is paid now and goods delivered later. The Hanafi school requires that the subject matter be precisely determinable in weight, measure, or count, and that it be an item that can be described without ambiguity.
This passage focuses on fish and certain containers.
2
Extract the primary ruling from the matn
The matn states: 'With known weight and known type, and the tast, qumquma, and khuffayn, unless not known by description. Not in that whose quantity and quality are unknown, like animals.' This establishes that for items that can be described (like fish and containers), both weight and type must be known.
The containers (tast, qumquma, khuffayn) are allowed if their description is known, even without weight.
3
Apply the ruling to fish: differentiate large vs. small
The commentary specifies that for large fish (kibar al-samak), both weight and type must be mentioned. For small fish (sighar), only known weight suffices, whether fresh or salted. This distinction is based on the practical ability to describe and the likelihood of variation.
The salted fish is explicitly mentioned as permissible because it is stored and available, as long as it does not become extinct.
4
Note the exception for animals
The matn excludes animals ('la fima la yu'lamu qadruhu wa sifatuhu kal-hayawan') because their hidden qualities (e.g., temperament, health) cannot be fully described, leading to gharar (excessive uncertainty). Salam in animals is not allowed in the Hanafi school, unlike the Shafi'i school.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on large cut fish
Abu Hanifa holds that salam in the meat of large fish that are cut into pieces (like meat) is not permissible, by analogy (qiyas) with salam in meat, which he does not allow. The comment from al-Hidayah implies that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is permissibility, but Abu Hanifa's view is recorded.
This shows that the Hanafi school has internal differences; the mufta bihi is the majority view that allows salam in large fish with weight and type specified, but Abu Hanifa's position is noteworthy for its consistency with his general rule on meat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب السلم

وزناً وضرباً معلومين ، والطَّرْتُ والقُمْقُمة، والخفِّين إلا إذا لم يعرف به ، لا فيما لا يُعْلَمُ قَدْرُهُ وصفتُهُ كالحيوان

(وزناً وضرباً معلومين) : أي لا بُدَّ أن يُذكر وزن معلوم، ونوع معلوم.
(والطَّسْتُ) ، والقُمْقُمةُ ) ، والخفِّين) إلا إذا لم يعرف به ) : أي بالصفة.
الا فيما لا يُعْلَمُ قَدْرُهُ وصفتُهُ كالحيوان) .
فأما المليح فإنه يدَّخرُ ويباع في الأسواق فلا ينقطع حتى لو كان ينقطع في بعض الأحيان لا يجوز ، كما صرَّحَ به العلامة الشامي، وغيره.
(وزناً وضرباً معلومين): هذا في كبار السمك ، وأمَّا الصغار منه فالسَلَمُ جائز فيه وزناً معلوماً طرياً كان أو مليحاً، ذكره البرْجَنْدِي، وعن أبي حنيفة له : إنه لا يجوز في لحم الكبار منها، وهي التي تقطع اعتباراً بالسَلَم في اللحم عنده، كذا في «الهداية).
Book of Sale, Chapter of Salam. (Ruling:) With known weight and known type, and the tast and the qumquma and the khuffayn, unless not known by description. Not in that whose quantity and quality are unknown like animals. (Commentary:) (With known weight and known type): i.e., it is necessary to mention known weight and known type. (And the tast, and the qumquma, and the khuffayn, unless not known by it): i.e., by description. Except for that whose quantity and quality are unknown like animals. As for the salted (fish), it is stored and sold in markets and does not become extinct; even if it becomes extinct at times, it is not permissible, as declared by Allamah al-Shami and others. (With known weight and known type): This applies to large fish. As for small fish, salam is permissible in them with known weight, whether fresh or salted, mentioned by al-Barjandi. And from Abu Hanifa: He does not permit it in the meat of large fish, which are cut, by analogy with salam in meat in his view, as in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on salam (advance payment sale) in fish and certain containers. The opening line is from the matn of al-Wiqayah. The commentary explains that for fish, both weight and type must be known for large fish; for small fish, only weight suffices. The condition of known weight and type ensures the subject matter is determined, preventing dispute. The exception for animals is because they vary greatly in hidden qualities. The commentary then addresses salted fish, noting that it remains available, so salam is valid; but if it becomes extinct, it is not. Finally, Abu Hanifa's view is cited: large fish cut into pieces are like meat, and salam in meat is not allowed according to him, so by analogy it is also not allowed in such fish. This shows the Hanafi school's detailed application of conditions for salam contracts.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): An advance payment sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later.
وزن معلوم (waznun ma'lum): A known weight that must be specified for the subject matter of salam.

Key Takeaway
Salam in fish is valid when weight and type are specified; for large fish cut into pieces, Abu Hanifa analogizes to meat, making it invalid.

Salam in Animals: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents Shafi'i's view allowing salam in animals and Hanafi's rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on salam in animals and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is invalid because even with description, hidden qualities cause dispute — the analogy to clothes is a qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

This passage presents a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether salam (advance payment sale) is valid for animals. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that animals can be sufficiently described, so salam should be valid by analogy to clothes. The Hanafi school counters that animals have gross inner disparity leading to disputes, and cites a hadith prohibiting salam in animals. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to handle analogical reasoning and the role of prophetic prohibitions in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding salam in animals and why. The text states: 'salam in animals is not allowed due to gross disparity in hidden qualities and because the Prophet forbade it.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that the opposing school is Imam al-Shafi'i. He allows salam in animals absolutely, arguing that animals become known through genus, species, and description.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i analogy: animals are like clothes because if genus, species, and description are specified, only slight disparity remains, and salam in clothes is valid by consensus. Therefore, salam in animals should also be valid.
The text mentions an additional argument about limbs (heads and trotters) being describable.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts with two arguments: (1) The analogy is invalid because animals have 'gross disparity' in hidden qualities like beauty, which humans cannot control, leading to disputes; this is qiyas ma'a al-fariq. (2) There is an explicit hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet forbade salam in animals.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that Hanafi jurists rule salam in animals impermissible, while Shafi'i jurists allow it. This affects actual contracts in communities following each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند الشافعي له يجوز جاز مطلقاً. حاصله أنَّ السَّلَمَ في الحيوان يجوزُ عنده ؛ لأنَّ الحيوان يصير معلوماً إذا بين جنسه كالإبل ونحوه، ونوعه كالبختي والعربي، ووصفه في الحيوان ؛ لأنه يتعين بذكرِ الجنس والنوع والصفة. قلنا : في ذلـك فـحـش التفاوت، (وأطرافه ) : كالرُّؤوس والأكارع كالسمين والهزال، والتفاوت بعد هذا البيان يسير، فأشبه الحيوان بالنّياب، فإنَّ فيها بعد ذكر الذرع والصفة والنوع لا يبقى إلا تفاوت يسير، فيجوز السلم فيها، فينبغي أن يجوز هاهنا أيضا. [١] قوله : قلنا؛ حاصلُهُ أنَّ قياس الحيوانِ على الثياب قياس مع الفارق ؛ لأنَّ في الحيوان بعد بيان الجنس والنوع والصفة تفاوتاً فاحشاً، باعتبار المعاني الباطنة كالصباحةِ والملاحة وغيرهما مما لا دخل فيه لأحد، فهذا التفاوت يفضي إلى المنازعة بخلاف الثياب، فإنّها من صنيع العباد. فإذا اتَّحد الصانع والآلةَ اتَّحد الصنيع، ولا يتفاوت في المالية إلا قليلاً، والحيوانُ صنيع الله ؛ وذلك يكون على ما يريدُهُ تعالى، فقد كان على وجه لا يوجد له نظير، وفي مثلِهِ لا يجوزُ السَّلَمُ بالاتفاق، هذا مُلَخَّصُ ما قرَّرهُ العلامةُ العَيْنِي ولنا أيضاً : ما أخرجه الحاكم في «المستدرك»، والدارقطني في «سننه»: عن ابن عباس أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : نهى عن السَّلَفِ في الحيوان (٢)، قال الحاكم : حديث صحيح الإسناد، ولم يخرجاه، ذكره العلامة الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في تخريجه».
And according to al-Shafi'i, he allows it absolutely. The summary is that salam in animals is allowed in his view because animals become known when its genus is specified like camels and the like, its species like Bakhti and Arabi, and its description in animals because it is determined by mentioning genus, species, and description. We said: In that there is gross disparity. (And its limbs) like heads and trotters, like fat and thin, and disparity after this description is slight, so it resembles animals to clothes, for in them after mentioning measure, description, and type, only slight disparity remains, so salam in them is allowed, so it should be allowed here too. [1] He said: We said; its summary is that analogizing animals to clothes is an analogy with a difference because in animals after mentioning genus, species, and description there is gross disparity, considering inner qualities like beauty and handsomeness and others over which none has control. So this disparity leads to dispute, unlike clothes, which are the handiwork of servants. If the maker and tool are uniform, the product is uniform, and does not vary in value except slightly. Animals are the handiwork of Allah, and that is as He wills, so it may be in a form that has no equal, and in such salam is not allowed by agreement. This is the summary of what Allamah al-Ayni stated. And we also have what al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak and al-Daraqutni in his Sunan from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (SAW) forbade salaf (salam) in animals. Al-Hakim said: This hadith has a sound chain but they did not record it. Mentioned by Allamah al-Zaylai in his Takhrij.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that salam in animals is valid because animals can be sufficiently defined by genus, species, and description. The Hanafi school responds that even with such description, there remains gross disparity due to hidden qualities like beauty, leading to inevitable disputes. The Hanafis also cite a hadith from Ibn Abbas (through al-Hakim and al-Daraqutni) that the Prophet forbade salam in animals. The commentator summarizes al-Ayni's argument: analogizing animals to clothes is invalid because clothes are uniform products of humans, while animals are creations of Allah and can vary extremely. The Shafi'i analogy from limbs (heads and trotters) is also rejected by the Hanafi view that such limbs still involve significant disparity. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that salam in land animals is not allowed, due to the hadith and rational argument.

Key Terms
القياس مع الفارق (al-qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a significant difference (fariq) between the original case and the new case.
سَلَم (salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance for a specifically described good to be delivered at a future date.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's primary evidence against salam in animals?
A) The analogy of animals to clothes
B) The hadith that the Prophet forbade salaf in animals
C) The consensus of the four schools
D) The difficulty in weighing animals

Key Takeaway
Salam in animals is impermissible in the Hanafi school due to the prophetic prohibition and the rational argument of gross hidden disparity, rejecting the Shafi'i analogy as qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Salam in Animal Limbs: Default Prohibition vs. Permissibility by Weight
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in animal limbs: default prohibition vs. permissibility by weight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi default ruling on salam in animal limbs and explain the condition under which the view of Fath al-Qadir permits it.

Core Idea
Salam in animal limbs is fasid by default due to variability, but permissible by weight after specification per al-Fath.

The permissibility of salam (forward sale) in animal parts like heads and trotters involves a known intra-Hanafi dispute. While the default ruling in the matn declares such contracts fasid because of excessive variability, a later authority, Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir, allowed them under specific conditions. This lesson examines both positions and the reasoning behind the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi default position
Identify the default ruling from the matn: salam in limbs (heads and trotters) is not allowed because they are highly variable, leading to dispute. The contract is fasid.
This is the position in the base text (likely from Al-Hidayah or similar).
2
Identify the opposing view from al-Fath
Note that Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir holds there is no objection to salam in heads and trotters by weight after specifying the type and meeting other conditions. He argues they are of one kind and do not vary excessively.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Compare the reasoning
The default view emphasizes that variability (tafawut) leads to dispute (niza'), similar to gharar. Al-Fath counters that when the type is specified and weight is known, the variability is not excessive (tafawut fahish).
The key issue is the degree of variability and how it is managed.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the permissive view from al-Fath, as it removes difficulty and is based on reasonable conditions. This is the position relied upon in later fatwa.
Tarjih authority: Ibn al-Humam (Fath al-Qadir), a late Hanafi authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢]قوله : وأطرافه ؛ وإنما لا يجوزُ السَّلَمُ فيها لكونها متفاوتة، وتفاوتها معتبر بين النَّاس، فتفضي إلى النزاع ، وقال في «الفتح» ) : وعندي لا بأس بالسلم في الرؤوس والأكارع وزنا بعد ذكر النوع وباقي الشروط، فإنَّها من جنس واحد، وحينئذ لا تتفاوت تفاوتاً فاحشاً. انتهى. [٣] قوله : والأكارع ؛ قال في «الصراح»: كراعُ بالضم: بارجه گوسفند و گاوو جزآن، وهو بمنزلة الوظيف في الفرس والبعير، وهو مشدق الساق، يذكر ويؤنث : أكرع وأكارع ج. انتهى.
[2] His statement: And its limbs; indeed salam in them is not allowed because they are variable, and their variability is significant among people, so it leads to dispute. He said in al-Fath: In my view, there is no objection to salam in heads and trotters by weight after mentioning the type and remaining conditions, for they are of one kind, and then they do not vary excessively. End. [3] His statement: And the akari'; he said in al-Sirah: Kurra' with damm: the lower leg of a sheep and cow and similar, and it is like the cannon bone of a horse and camel, and it is the shank; it is used as masculine and feminine; plural: akru' and akari'. End.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on salam in animal limbs, specifically heads and trotters (akari'). The default Hanafi position is that salam in these limbs is not allowed because they are highly variable in size and quality, leading to disputes between buyer and seller. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: the author of Fath al-Qadir (likely Ibn al-Humam) holds that there is no harm in salam in heads and trotters by weight after specifying the type and meeting other conditions, arguing that they belong to one kind and do not vary excessively. This shows a more lenient view within the Hanafi school. The commentary also provides a lexical definition of 'akari' (plural of kurrah) as the shank of animals, confirming subject matter.

Key Terms
الأكارع (al-akari'): Plural of kurrah, meaning the lower legs or shanks of animals (sheep, cow, etc.), similar to cannon bones in horses/camels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They must be fresh
B) Weight must be known after specifying type
C) They must be from sheep only
D) No conditions are necessary

Key Takeaway
Salam in animal limbs is fasid by default, but the mufta bihi view permits it by weight after specifying type, as per Fath al-Qadir.
